  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_81957f44-0ac6-4224-8d66-e477b938eaeb'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12995047653201377732">A breathtaking collection of reflections from one of the world's best loved storytellers, Paulo Coelho. In this riveting collection of thoughts and stories, Paulo Coelho, the author of 'The Alchemist', offers his personal reflections on a wide range of subjects from archery and music to elegance, traveling and the nature of good and evil. An old woman explains to her grand</span>
  <span id="freeText12995047653201377732" style="display:none">A breathtaking collection of reflections from one of the world's best loved storytellers, Paulo Coelho. In this riveting collection of thoughts and stories, Paulo Coelho, the author of 'The Alchemist', offers his personal reflections on a wide range of subjects from archery and music to elegance, traveling and the nature of good and evil. An old woman explains to her grandson how a mere pencil can show him the path to happiness...instructions on how to climb a mountain reveal the secret to making your dreams a reality!the story of Ghengis Khan and the Falcon that teaches about the folly of anger - and the art of friendship!a pianist who performs an example in fulfilling your destiny!the author learns three important lessons when he goes to the rescue of a man in the street - Paulo shows us how life has lessons for us in the greatest, smallest and most unusual of experiences. 'Like the Flowing River' includes jewel-like fables, packed with meaning and retold in Coelho's inimitable style. Sharing his thoughts on spirituality, life and ethics, Paulo touches you with his philosophy and invites you to go on an exciting journey of your own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12995047653201377732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17109105670539956666">Ser Como o Rio que Flui‬ = Like the Flowing River, Paulo Coelho<br/><br/>In this collection of thoughts and stories, Coelho, author of 'The Alchemist', offers his personal reflections on a range of subjects from archery and music to elegance, travelling and the nature of good and evil. 'Like the Flowing River' also includes jewel-like fables, packed with meaning and retold in Coelho's inimitable style.<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه جولای سال 2006 میلادی<br/><br/>عنوان: چون رود جاری باش؛ نویسنده: پائولو کوئیلو (کوئلیو)؛ مت</span>
  <span id="freeText17109105670539956666" style="display:none">Ser Como o Rio que Flui‬ = Like the Flowing River, Paulo Coelho<br /><br />In this collection of thoughts and stories, Coelho, author of 'The Alchemist', offers his personal reflections on a range of subjects from archery and music to elegance, travelling and the nature of good and evil. 'Like the Flowing River' also includes jewel-like fables, packed with meaning and retold in Coelho's inimitable style.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه جولای سال 2006 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: چون رود جاری باش؛ نویسنده: پائولو کوئیلو (کوئلیو)؛ مترجم: آرش حجازی؛ تهران، کاروان، چاپ اول 1385؛ در 322ص؛ چاپ دوم تا چهارم 1386؛ چاپ هشتم 1387؛ شابک 9789648497588؛ موضوع: داستانهای کوتاه از نویسندگان برزیلی - سده 20م<br /><br />کتاب «چون رود جاری باش»؛ مجموعه‌ ای از «قصه‌ ها»،‌ «باورها»، و «دیدگاههای» نویسنده ی نام آشنای خوانشگران ایرانی «پائولو کوئلیو»، و برشی در پهنای کالبدشناسی کنشهای ادبی ایشان،‌ و بازتابی زیبا از گستره‌ ی آفرینش‌های این نویسنده‌ ی برزیلی ست؛ هماره قلمش جاوید خواهد ماند؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267741654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7446726147495976324">Oh, why do I even bother anymore with Coelho? His books are easy (read: shallow) reads but leave a bad aftertaste, much like how I feel after I'm done bingeing on junk food. Write about spirituality in a stripped, simplified way, sprinkle in some pseudo-intellectualism and voila - you get a world famous author with little substance. Coelho should be taught two things: one is that nuanced writing is a much better approach in philosophizing, and two, it would do the readers good if he could tone d</span>
  <span id="freeText7446726147495976324" style="display:none">Oh, why do I even bother anymore with Coelho? His books are easy (read: shallow) reads but leave a bad aftertaste, much like how I feel after I'm done bingeing on junk food. Write about spirituality in a stripped, simplified way, sprinkle in some pseudo-intellectualism and voila - you get a world famous author with little substance. Coelho should be taught two things: one is that nuanced writing is a much better approach in philosophizing, and two, it would do the readers good if he could tone down his ego a bit. There's something really bothersome about a writer who keeps wanting to show how enlightened he is. I hope I don't forget that and pick up another one of his work after this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7446726147495976324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12717381671254427587">Each Christmas, we have an exchange of gifts. The actual exchange of gifts take place during the annual Christmas party. Last Christmas (2011), I was collecting Nicholas Sparks' books. This Christmas (2012), I was collecting Paulo Coelho books. So, naturally, I wrote down *Paulo Coelho books* on my wish list. To cut the story short, I received</span>
  <span id="freeText12717381671254427587" style="display:none">Each Christmas, we have an exchange of gifts. The actual exchange of gifts take place during the annual Christmas party. Anyway, all employees were asked to create a *wish list*. The wish list contained all (or some) of the things that we would like to receive for Christmas. Last Christmas (2011), I was collecting Nicholas Sparks' books. This Christmas (2012), I was collecting Paulo Coelho books. So, naturally, I wrote down *Paulo Coelho books* on my wish list. To cut the story short, I received the book 'Like the Flowing River'. <br /><br />I am not a huge fan of short stories. Yet, like only Paulo Coelho could, he transported me to different worlds with an open mind and an open heart. Some of the compilations of thoughts that struck me the most was 'Music in the Chapel', 'Genghis Khan and his Falcon', 'The Dead Man Wore Pajamas' and 'Norma and the Good Things'. In lieu with the latter story, I have decided to make my own planner marked with wonderful inventions and happenings that ought to be celebrated. :)<br /><br />If you would like to take a break from all of the novels and fiction that you read, you will find 'Like the Flowing River' very refreshing. </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Junix Jerald" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8673863-junix-jerald"><img alt="Junix Jerald" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372442951p2/8673863.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309177922?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Junix Jerald" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Junix Jerald" href="/user/show/8673863-junix-jerald">Junix Jerald</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18304934-like-the-flowing-river">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309177922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer198796283431723632">Like the Flowing River is a collection of Paulo Coelho’s stories and articles which were published in different newspapers around the world.<br/><br/>Like the Flowing River is definitely one of Coelho’s best, for me. It contained his thoughts and reflections on different things—from the story of the pencil to a piece of bread that fell wrong side up. I’m amused at how he sees the Universe. How he comes up with various realizations out of the simplest things that happen in his life.<br/><br/>This proves that Paulo C</span>
  <span id="freeText198796283431723632" style="display:none">Like the Flowing River is a collection of Paulo Coelho’s stories and articles which were published in different newspapers around the world.<br /><br />Like the Flowing River is definitely one of Coelho’s best, for me. It contained his thoughts and reflections on different things—from the story of the pencil to a piece of bread that fell wrong side up. I’m amused at how he sees the Universe. How he comes up with various realizations out of the simplest things that happen in his life.<br /><br />This proves that Paulo Coelho really has a profound understanding of the Universe. The stories and articles were compiled in a such a way that the reader would not have a hard time reading them. Most of these articles made me think of the different possibilities that may happen in my life.<br /><br />There were a hundred or so stories and articles contained in Coelho’s Like the Flowing River, and here are the ones that I liked:<br /><br /> Prepared for Battle, But with a Few Doubts<br /> The Story of the Pencil *<br /> How to Climb Mountains<br /> Genghis Khan and His Falcon<br /> How One Thing Can Contain Everything *<br /> The Dead Man Wore Pyjamas<br /> The Solitary Piece of Coal *<br /> The Piece of Bread That Fell Wrong Side Up *<br /> Of Books and Libraries<br /> Prague, 1891<br /> A Visitor Arrives from Morocco<br /> The Moment of Dawn *<br /> A Man Lying on the Ground *<br /> Raj Tells Me a Story *<br /> Copacabana, Rio de Janeiro<br /> Statutes for the New Millennium *<br /> Destroying and Rebuilding<br /> Travelling Differently<br /> A Fairy Tale *<br /> The Australian and the Newspaper Ad *<br /> The Tears of the Desert *<br /> Rome: Isabella Returns from Nepal *<br /> In the Blue Mountains<br /> The Cloud and the Sand Dune *<br /> Norma and the Good Things *<br /> In San Diego Harbour, California<br /> The Soldier in the Forest *<br /> The Funny Thing About Human Beings *<br /> Who Would Like This Twenty-Dollar Bill? *<br /> The Art of Trying<br /> My Father-in-law, Christiano Oiticica<br /> Thank You, President Bush *<br /> The Catholic and the Muslim *<br /> Evil Wants Good to Prevail<br /> The Old Lady in Copacabana *<br /> Remaining Open to Love *<br /> Believing in the Impossible<br /> Some Final Prayers *<br /><br />* The ones that had a great impact on me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="198796283431723632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1563236418" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1563236418" />
    <a title="Annette mathews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35734106-annette-mathews"><img alt="Annette mathews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603723533p2/35734106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1563236418?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annette mathews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annette mathews" href="/user/show/35734106-annette-mathews">Annette mathews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35734106-annette-mathews?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35734106-annette-mathews?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563236418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12780729499259874650">I will admit one thing,if not for my brother , i would not have read this book or for the matter any books of his. <br/>My friends used to recommend his books, but i had always stayed away from his books. From what i have heard, his books always sounded Philosophical, which for me is the other name for Boring . I have never been into books of that category. I stay away from Self Help books. I tried reading it once since an avid reader should read all types of Genre. But sadly , it resulted in a "read</span>
  <span id="freeText12780729499259874650" style="display:none">I will admit one thing,if not for my brother , i would not have read this book or for the matter any books of his. <br />My friends used to recommend his books, but i had always stayed away from his books. From what i have heard, his books always sounded Philosophical, which for me is the other name for Boring . I have never been into books of that category. I stay away from Self Help books. I tried reading it once since an avid reader should read all types of Genre. But sadly , it resulted in a "reading slump" phase. From that time on wards, i have strongly stayed away from those kind of books.<br />My brother unfortunately for him, told me that he had come across many novels in his University Library . My university, on the other hand only had books related to engineering and stuffs like that . My brother took the first book , which caught his eye from the library to stop my incessant pestering .Guess what , he took a book which i was least likely to read. I was thinking whether to waste my time reading this book ,coz i know i would be dropping this book at some point of time.<br />Anyway i couldn't see the book being abandoned since my brother went all the way to place which he rarely goes,for me. Guess what , I finished reading it . I was pleasantly surprised by this book. I am in short of words to express how i felt while reading it . You look at the world in a different light once you start reading this book . Now , i sound so philosophical . But clearly Paulo Coleho expresses it in a way which no one ever has .He just puts things differently.<br /><br />This particular book of his is a collection of Short stories of his life.<br /><br />I am a religious person and this one particular story lingered in my mind for a long time .<br /><br /><b>An old illiterate Arab used to pray with such fervor each night that the wealthy owner of the great caravan decided to summon him so as to talk to him.<br />“Why do you pray with such devotion? How do you know God exists when you don’t even know how to read?”<br />“I do know, sir. I can read everything that the Great Celestial Father writes.”<br />“But how?”<br />The humble servant explained:<br />“When you receive a letter from someone far away, how do you recognize the writer?”<br />“By the handwriting.”<br />“When you receive a jewel, how do you know who made it?”<br />“By the goldsmith’s mark.”<br />“When you hear animals moving about near the tent, how do you know if it was a sheep or a horse or an ox?”<br />“By its footprints,” replied the owner, surprised at all these questions.<br />The old man invited him to come outside with him and showed him the sky.<br />“Neither the things written up there nor the desert down below could have been made or written by the hand of man.” </b><br /><br />This is just one story .This book is packed with such stories like this . All different from one another. If you like this one story, then read this book . Paulo is a wise person and it is known in the stories he shares with us . </span>
  <a data-text-id="12780729499259874650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137505424" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137505424" />
    <a title="Fatima Al-Quwaie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3835387-fatima-al-quwaie"><img alt="Fatima Al-Quwaie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438120176p2/3835387.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137505424?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fatima Al-Quwaie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fatima Al-Quwaie" href="/user/show/3835387-fatima-al-quwaie">Fatima Al-Quwaie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137505424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18166035285175802668">I never thought that a man can really be so profound and inspiring even in his daily life, until I read Paulo Coelho’s Like the Flowing River.<br/><br/>Before I read this book, I have read Coelho’s book “The Alchemist”, and just credited him for a wonderful work of art. But after reading this book, I discovered that Coelho is not only a masterful writer but also a man full of wisdom in real life.<br/><br/>Like the Flowing River is a gleaning of accounts of his experiences, stories he had been told and thoughts than</span>
  <span id="freeText18166035285175802668" style="display:none">I never thought that a man can really be so profound and inspiring even in his daily life, until I read Paulo Coelho’s Like the Flowing River.<br /><br />Before I read this book, I have read Coelho’s book “The Alchemist”, and just credited him for a wonderful work of art. But after reading this book, I discovered that Coelho is not only a masterful writer but also a man full of wisdom in real life.<br /><br />Like the Flowing River is a gleaning of accounts of his experiences, stories he had been told and thoughts than he had while traveling from one country to another. It would put you in Coelho’s shoes from the time he was just a boy dreaming to be a writer, to the time he actually became one of the widest read writers in the world, and the experiences he had between these points in time. It will bring you inside his mind and read his reflections on living and dying, destiny and choice, and love lost and found.<br /><br />After reading the book, you will have a new perspective in life. You will appreciate little but important things you haven’t noticed before. You will enjoy living more.<br /><br />A read that will definitely make you smile! </span>
  <a data-text-id="18166035285175802668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18188452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18188452" />
    <a title="Bunga Mawar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1007892-bunga-mawar"><img alt="Bunga Mawar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328585199p2/1007892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18188452?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bunga Mawar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bunga Mawar" href="/user/show/1007892-bunga-mawar">Bunga Mawar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1007892-bunga-mawar?shelf=stated-as-nonfiction">stated-as-nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1007892-bunga-mawar?shelf=buku-boleh-pinjem">buku-boleh-pinjem</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18188452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6845971516828495530">Dari Bab "The Prayer that I Forgot", demen banget dah gua... <br/><br/><i>Lord, protect our doubts, because Doubt is a way of praying.   <span id="freeText6845971516828495530" style="display:none">Dari Bab "The Prayer that I Forgot", demen banget dah gua... <br /><br /><i>Lord, protect our doubts, because Doubt is a way of praying. It is Doubt that makes us grow because it forces us to look fearlessly at the many answers that exist to one question. And in order for this to be possible...<br /><br />Lord, protect our decisions, because making Decision is a way of praying. Give us the courage after our doubts, to be able to choose between one road and another. May our YES always be a YES and our NO always be a NO. Once we have chosen our road, may we never look back nor allow our soul to be eaten away by remorse. And in order for this to be possible...<br /><br />Lord, protect our action, because Action is a way of praying. May our daily bread be the best result of the very best that we carry within us. May we, through work and Action, share a little of the love we receive. And in order to make this to be possible...<br /><br />Lord, protect our dreams, because to Dream is a way of praying. Make sure that, regardless of our age or our circumstances, we are capable of keeping alight in our heart the sacred flame of hope and perseverance. And in order for this to be possible...<br /><br />Lord, give us enthusiasm, because Enthusiasm is a way of praying. It is what binds us to the Heavens and to Earth, to grown-ups and to children; it is what tells us that our desires are important and deserve our best efforts. It is Enthusiasm that reaffirms us that everything is possible, as long as we are totally committed to what we are doing. And in order for this to be possible...<br /><br />Lord, protect us, because Life is the only way we have of making manifest Your miracle. May the earth continue to transfom seeds into wheat, may we continue to transmute wheat into bread. And this is only possible if we have Love; therefore, do not leave us in solitude. Always give us Your company, and the company of men and women who have doubts, who act and dream and feel enthusiasm, and who live each day as if it were totally dedicated to Your glory.</i><br /></span>

<div id="review_656870764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/656870764" />
    <a title="Rosie Nguyễn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15715846-rosie-nguy-n"><img alt="Rosie Nguyễn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393381224p2/15715846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/656870764?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosie Nguyễn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosie Nguyễn" href="/user/show/15715846-rosie-nguy-n">Rosie Nguyễn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer656870764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18379134785029819760">I don't know how to explain my love for this book. It was a surprised gift from a new lovely friend, and I brought it with me to a short vacation in a beautiful island. Early in a morning, I had a long swim on the deserted beach, then lied down under the shade of almond trees, reading the book, pondering my life, then swimming again. In front of me, on the other side of the sea, Hongkong city resting quietly, glittering in the morning sun rays shining through grey clouds. What a wonderful moment</span>
  <span id="freeText18379134785029819760" style="display:none">I don't know how to explain my love for this book. It was a surprised gift from a new lovely friend, and I brought it with me to a short vacation in a beautiful island. Early in a morning, I had a long swim on the deserted beach, then lied down under the shade of almond trees, reading the book, pondering my life, then swimming again. In front of me, on the other side of the sea, Hongkong city resting quietly, glittering in the morning sun rays shining through grey clouds. What a wonderful moment I had with this book. <br /><br />The book is a combination of short stories the writer came across here and there, of events happened to him and his thoughts about them. It strikes me that these events are nothing special, petty even, events that happen from time to time in one's daily life, a walk in the forest, a gardening work... While many of us passing through life, never pay attention to such events, Paulo Coelho does, reflecting, and noting down his thoughts. That is what matters.<br /><br />Among these stories, I was especially impressed by the one about the author's childhood dream to be a writer. When he was small, he told his mother that he wanted to be a writer. His mother replied: "your father is an engineer, why don't you be an engineer that writes". My mom told me the same, replacing engineer by office staff. But he didn't want to be an engineer who writes. Neither do I. Paulo Coelho represents a man who strives for his life, who lives his dreams, who believes in miracles and spreading his love for God, for human being, for beauty of the earth. That's how I want to lead my life. And I'm gonna work my butt off to live that way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18379134785029819760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149237101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16706612275377991484"> My friend told me to read this book about a year ago but I was never really interested in reading. I never found the right book to read. This summer I read a book for Paulo Coelho and I loved it. So I kept buying his books and reading them. His books are really different. They are all about life and how we choose our path. Some are all about love, destiny, and death. After I read most of his books I decided to start reading this book ''Like the Flowing River''. It made a great impact on the way</span>
  <span id="freeText16706612275377991484" style="display:none"> My friend told me to read this book about a year ago but I was never really interested in reading. I never found the right book to read. This summer I read a book for Paulo Coelho and I loved it. So I kept buying his books and reading them. His books are really different. They are all about life and how we choose our path. Some are all about love, destiny, and death. After I read most of his books I decided to start reading this book ''Like the Flowing River''. It made a great impact on the way i think of life. It showed me that life has a bright side that no one ever looks at. Coelho's books aren't silly stories, they are stories with meanings. This book has short stories about many different people that Coelho met during his life. They are either family, friends, or strangers. It talks about the incidents and problems that happened with these people and how it taught them a lesson. <br /><br />One of my favorite quotes in this book that Coelho mentioned was ''These days people think a lot of their future and forget to live their present.'' This sentence really touched me. It has so many meanings and its in every persons life. It made me more optimistic and now I always keep in mind that at the end no one is taking anything with them, therefore enjoy your life to the fullest and make the best of each second. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16706612275377991484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17655265281712992278">This is a great book of meditations large and small in the form of stories and true vignettes from the life of the author. I recommend keeping it on your nightstand and reading just one or two stories before you go to bed--you'll sleep well. If you are familiar with Coelho's works, you'll recognize the "warrior of the light" and the reference to "personal legends" (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/865.The_Alchemist' title='The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Alchemist</a>). The collection is a testament to Coelho's expansive horizon (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4006.The_Valkyries_An_Encounter_with_Angels' title='The Valkyries An Encounter with Angels by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Valkyries: An Encounter with Angels</a>) and wi</span>
  <span id="freeText17655265281712992278" style="display:none">This is a great book of meditations large and small in the form of stories and true vignettes from the life of the author. I recommend keeping it on your nightstand and reading just one or two stories before you go to bed--you'll sleep well. If you are familiar with Coelho's works, you'll recognize the "warrior of the light" and the reference to "personal legends" (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/865.The_Alchemist" title="The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alchemist</a>). <span id="freeTextContainer13957804599243383862">I had read The Alchemist and Brida by Paulo Coelho before and had loved them both. Those books left me with messages that changed my life. Given my previous experiences with Coelho's books, I was pretty excited about Like a Flowing River too, until I read a few reviews (mostly negative) of the book. I nevertheless did not put the book away and I am glad I didn't.<br/><br/>Yes, there are a few thoughts in the book that give you a blah feeling, however the book has some hidden gems of inspiration that make </span>
  <span id="freeText13957804599243383862" style="display:none">I had read The Alchemist and Brida by Paulo Coelho before and had loved them both. Those books left me with messages that changed my life. Given my previous experiences with Coelho's books, I was pretty excited about Like a Flowing River too, until I read a few reviews (mostly negative) of the book. I nevertheless did not put the book away and I am glad I didn't.<br /><br />Yes, there are a few thoughts in the book that give you a blah feeling, however the book has some hidden gems of inspiration that make reading it worthwhile. I am sure that not all the stories and thoughts shared will resonate with everyone but then you will still find something or the other in this book that you will cherish for the years to come.<br /><br />I will keep this book in my library for life, reading out some of the thoughts therein to myself and a few others to my nephew as he grows up.</span>

<div id="review_1297090555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297090555" />
    <a title="Ahmed R. Rashwan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37690097-ahmed-r-rashwan"><img alt="Ahmed R. Rashwan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541047821p2/37690097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297090555?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed R. Rashwan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed R. Rashwan" href="/user/show/37690097-ahmed-r-rashwan">Ahmed R. Rashwan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297090555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8827634056836188288">There are only a few authors; or for fairness sake in this situation, books, that can annoy me as much as <i>Like the Flowing River</i> has.<br/><br/>I understand that Paulo Coelho sees himself as this mysterious magical being, but it just always comes out as condescending and patronizing; even self-centered and narcissistic at times. I mean this guy really needs to take a break and understand the world can function just as well without his egoistic and narrow-minded view of life.<br/><br/>To some, it might seem audacious</span>
  <span id="freeText8827634056836188288" style="display:none">There are only a few authors; or for fairness sake in this situation, books, that can annoy me as much as <i>Like the Flowing River</i> has.<br /><br />I understand that Paulo Coelho sees himself as this mysterious magical being, but it just always comes out as condescending and patronizing; even self-centered and narcissistic at times. I mean this guy really needs to take a break and understand the world can function just as well without his egoistic and narrow-minded view of life.<br /><br />To some, it might seem audacious of me to say Paulo Coelho has a narrow-minded view of life as he always tries to encompass as much religions, belief systems and ideologies into his writing. But if you look at things from a bigger and wider perspective, Paulo's writing style can sometimes offer you a glimpse into his hypocritical tendencies. Coelho is smart in how he does this umbrella style of encompassing people from all walks of life into his writing, but the reality is that at many times, if reading his work objectively, you will be able to spot the hypocrisy and deceit in it all.<br /><br />Face it Mr. Coelho, not everyone sees the world the way you do, and they in no way have to! Paulo's mistake is that he forgot to add one belief system in his all-encompassing charlatanism; and that is atheism, whose followers see the world with as much beauty as his fairy avid followers see their Hogwarts fashioned universe.<br /><br />Which brings me to the question of why most of Paulo Coelho's magicians, main characters, plot drivers, story tellers, musicians, etc. are of the female genre. A way to get into more women's pants perhaps? Does not seem highly unlikely if we're going to be completely frank.<br /><br />The only reason this book gets two stars rather one star, is because of the <b>very</b> rare cases where Paulo Coelho actually writes a good, believable, sensical and relatable story, and because of his incorporating other people's writing who I must offer my respects to with an additional star (Lao Tzu comes to mind).<br /><br />The first book I ever read was by Mr. Paulo Coelho (which by the way I absolutely loved and always recommend) and indeed I have rated and praised some of his work highly, yet it seems that I have lost my tolerance against his world and religious views, which I do not only disagree with, but even to a high degree unfortunately but genuinely abhor. <br /><br />My God man, the world is much more far reaching than God, Love (capitalized) and women... </span>
  <a data-text-id="8827634056836188288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3260557576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3260557576" />
    <a title="Nari Wahlang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58783093-nari-wahlang"><img alt="Nari Wahlang" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594964149p2/58783093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3260557576?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nari Wahlang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nari Wahlang" href="/user/show/58783093-nari-wahlang">Nari Wahlang</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3260557576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16337832065744412569">Honestly speaking I actually quite enjoyed this book. I loved Coelho's writing and I loved the fact that he doesn't make everyday things sound boring as hell. Like how I like to quote Pam Beesley, "There's a lot of beauty in ordinary things. Isn't that kind of the point?" Yes I will forever be a fan of The Office and I actually do believe in what Pam Beesley says. <br/><br/>My only problem with the book is that there were way to many stories so the really heartfelt, touching and impactful stories were mix</span>
  <span id="freeText16337832065744412569" style="display:none">Honestly speaking I actually quite enjoyed this book. I loved Coelho's writing and I loved the fact that he doesn't make everyday things sound boring as hell. Like how I like to quote Pam Beesley, "There's a lot of beauty in ordinary things. Isn't that kind of the point?" Yes I will forever be a fan of The Office and I actually do believe in what Pam Beesley says. <br /><br />My only problem with the book is that there were way to many stories so the really heartfelt, touching and impactful stories were mixed with the rather average and not so great ones that by the time you're done with the book, you kind of forget which stories you loved in the first place. <br /><br />It's an easy read and if you're feeling a little down, I suggest you give this book a read. It's light, it's touching, it's inspirational, it's basically a book that looks on the brighter side of life and honestly speaking, at a time like this, I think we all need a little optimism in our lives. Even though you might not relate to some stories, there will definitely be a story in there for you. <br /><br />So I'd give this book a 4 star rating out of 5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16337832065744412569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a8UXXH1mKap0sQiexTblDx69pqKsBven198G7/tMqv2KjIrbZFVSwFLlj20EdMESLG4T+7ZJ65FdBwoRbB2ZRA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho">About Paulo Coelho</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201840056p3/566.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8944782562570006372">The Brazilian author PAULO COELHO was born in 1947 in the city of Rio de Janeiro. Before dedicating his life completely to literature, he worked as theatre director and actor, lyricist and journalist. In 1986, PAULO COELHO did the pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella, an experience later to be documented in his book The Pilgrimage. In the following year, COELHO published The Alchemist. Slow in</span>
  <span id="freeText8944782562570006372" style="display:none">The Brazilian author PAULO COELHO was born in 1947 in the city of Rio de Janeiro. Before dedicating his life completely to literature, he worked as theatre director and actor, lyricist and journalist. In 1986, PAULO COELHO did the pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella, an experience later to be documented in his book The Pilgrimage. In the following year, COELHO published The Alchemist. Slow initial sales convinced his first publisher to drop the novel, but it went on to become one of the best selling Brazilian books of all time. Other titles include Brida (1990), The Valkyries (1992), By the river Piedra I sat Down and Wept (1994), the collection of his best columns published in the Brazilian newspaper Folha de São Paulo entitle Maktub (1994), the compilation of texts Phrases (1995), The Fifth Mountain (1996), Manual of a Warrior of Light (1997), Veronika decides to die (1998), The Devil and Miss Prym (2000), the compilation of traditional tales in Stories for parents, children and grandchildren (2001), Eleven Minutes (2003), The Zahir (2005), The Witch of Portobello (2006) and Winner Stands Alone (to be released in 2009). During the months of March, April, May and June 2006, Paulo Coelho traveled to celebrate the 20th anniversary of his pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella in 1986. He also held surprise book signings - announced one day in advance - in some cities along the way, to have a chance to meet his readers. In ninety days of pilgrimage the author traveled around the globe and took the famous Transiberrian train that took him to Vladivostok. During this experience Paulo Coelho launched his blog Walking the Path - The Pilgrimage in order to share with his readers his impressions. Since this first blog Paulo Coelho has expanded his presence in the internet with his daily blogs in Wordpress, Myspace &amp; Facebook. He is equally present in media sharing sites such as Youtube and Flickr, offering on a regular basis not only texts but also videos and pictures to his readers. From this intensive interest and use of the Internet sprang his bold new project: The Experimental Witch where he invites his readers to adapt to the screen his book The Witch of Portobello. Indeed Paulo Coelho is a firm believer of Internet as a new media and is the first Best-selling author to actively support online free distribution of his work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8944782562570006372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
